					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Western Ibero-Romance language</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the Romance language spoken in the region of Galicia, northwestern Spain. For the extinct Iberian Celtic language, see <a href="/wiki/Gallaecian" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallaecian">Gallaecian</a>. For the language spoken in the Eastern European region of Galizia, see <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Polish_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Lesser Polish dialect">Lesser Polish dialect</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_dialects" title="Ukrainian dialects">Ukrainian dialects</a>.</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Galego" redirects here. For the creation myth from Bugis, Indonesia, see <a href="/wiki/Sureq_Galigo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sureq Galigo">Sureq Galigo</a>. For the type of primate, see <a href="/wiki/Galago" title="Galago">Galago</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

color: black; background-color:  #c9ffd9;">Galician</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader" style="font-size:110%; color: black; background-color:  #c9ffd9;"><span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">galego</i></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Pronunciation</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="gl-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Galician" title="Help:IPA/Galician">&#91;ɡaˈleɣʊ&#93;</a></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Region</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and adjacent areas in <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Ethnicity</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Galician_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician people">Galician</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Native speakers</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">2.4 million&#160;(2012)<sup id="cite_ref-e18_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e18-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><br />58% of the population of Galicia (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1.56 million) are <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">L1</a> speakers (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; <ul style="line-height:100%; margin-left:1.35em;padding-left:0"><li>
<a href="/wiki/Italic_languages" title="Italic languages">Italic</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Latino-Faliscan_languages" title="Latino-Faliscan languages">Latino-Faliscan</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Italo-Western_languages" title="Italo-Western languages">Italo-Western</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">Western Romance</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Ibero-Romance_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibero-Romance languages">Ibero-Romance</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">West Iberian</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><b>Galician</b></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Early forms</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><div style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a>

</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:Lang_Status_80-VU.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Lang_Status_80-VU.svg/320px-Lang_Status_80-VU.svg.png" decoding="async" width="320" height="96" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Lang_Status_80-VU.svg/480px-Lang_Status_80-VU.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Lang_Status_80-VU.svg/640px-Lang_Status_80-VU.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="153" /></a></span><div style="text-align:left;"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><span style="font-size:85%;">Galician is classified as Vulnerable by the UNESCO <a href="/wiki/Atlas_of_the_World%27s_Languages_in_Danger" title="Atlas of the World&#39;s Languages in Danger">Atlas of the World's Languages in Danger</a>     <sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></span></div></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-below noprint selfref" style="background-color:#E7E7FF;padding:0.3em 0.5em;text-align:left;line-height:1.3;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA#Rendering_issues" title="Help:IPA">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Galician</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/ʃ/: &#39;sh&#39; in &#39;shy&#39;">ʃ</span><span title="/ən/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">endonym</a>: <i lang="gl">galego</i>), also known as <b>Galego</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">Western Ibero-Romance</a> language. Around 2.4&#160;million people have at least some degree of competence in the language, mainly in <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> located in northwestern Spain, where it has official status along with <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>. The language is also spoken in some border zones of the neighbouring Spanish regions of <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a>, as well as by Galician migrant communities in the rest of Spain, in Latin America including <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, the United States, Switzerland and elsewhere in Europe.
</p><p>Modern Galician is classified as part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">West Iberian languages</a> group, a family of <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>. Galician evolved locally from <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> and developed from what modern scholars have called <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a>. The earliest document written integrally in the local Galician variety dates back to 1230, although the subjacent Romance permeates most written Latin local charters since the High Middle Ages, being specially noteworthy in personal and place names recorded in those documents, as well as in terms originated in languages other than Latin. The earliest reference to Galician-Portuguese as an international language of culture dates to 1290, in the <i>Regles de Trobar</i> by Catalan author <a href="/wiki/Jofre_de_Foix%C3%A0" title="Jofre de Foixà">Jofre de Foixà</a>, where it is simply called Galician (<i>gallego</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998142_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998142-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dialectal divergences are observable between the northern and southern forms of Galician-Portuguese in 13th-century texts but the two <a href="#Dialects">dialects</a> were similar enough to maintain a high level of cultural unity until the middle of the 14th century, producing the medieval <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_lyric" title="Galician-Portuguese lyric">Galician-Portuguese lyric</a>. The divergence has continued to this day, most frequently due to innovations in Portuguese,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> producing the modern languages of Galician and Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
The <a href="/wiki/Lexicon" title="Lexicon">lexicon</a> of Galician is predominantly of <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> extraction, although it also contains a moderate number of words of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Galician_words_of_Germanic_origin" title="List of Galician words of Germanic origin">Germanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Galician_words_of_Celtic_origin" title="List of Galician words of Celtic origin">Celtic</a> origin, among other <a href="/wiki/Substratum_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Substratum (linguistics)">substrates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adstrate" class="mw-redirect" title="Adstrate">adstrates</a>, having also received, mainly via Spanish, a number of nouns from <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Arabic" class="mw-redirect" title="Andalusian Arabic">Andalusian Arabic</a>.
</p><p>The language is officially regulated in Galicia by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Galician_Academy" title="Royal Galician Academy">Royal Galician Academy</a>. Other organizations without institutional support, such as the <a href="/wiki/Galician_Association_of_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician Association of Language">Galician Association of Language</a> consider Galician and Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Reintegrationism" title="Reintegrationism">two forms of the Galician-Portuguese language</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and other minoritary organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Galician_Academy_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Galician Academy of the Portuguese Language">Galician Academy of the Portuguese Language</a> believe that Galician should be considered part of the Portuguese language for a wider international usage and level of 'normalization'.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification_and_relation_with_Portuguese">Classification and relation with Portuguese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Classification and relation with Portuguese"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese#Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese §&#160;Language</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif/220px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif/330px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif/440px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif 2x" data-file-width="806" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>Map showing the historical retreat and expansion of Galician (Galician and Portuguese) within the context of its linguistic neighbors between the year 1000 and 2000</figcaption></figure>
<p>Modern Galician and Portuguese originated from a common medieval ancestor designated variously by modern linguists as <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a> (or as Medieval Galician, Medieval Portuguese, Old Galician or Old Portuguese). This common ancestral stage developed from <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> in the territories of the old <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Kingdom of Galicia">Kingdom of Galicia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Portugal">Northern Portugal</a>, as a Western <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance language">Romance language</a>. In the 13th century it became a written and cultivated language with two main varieties,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200317_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200317-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> but during the 14th century the standards of these varieties, Galician and Portuguese, began to diverge, as Portuguese became the official language of the independent <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a> and its chancellery, while Galician was the language of the scriptoria of the lawyers, noblemen and churchmen of the Kingdom of Galicia, then integrated in the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">crown of Castile</a> and open to influence from Spanish language, culture, and politics. During the 16th century the Galician language stopped being used in legal documentation, becoming de facto an oral language spoken by the vast majority of the Galicians, but having just some minor written use in lyric, theatre and private letters.
</p><p>It was not until the 18th century that linguists elaborated the first Galician dictionaries, and the language did not recover a proper literature until the 19th century; only since the last quarter of the 20th century is it taught in schools and used in lawmaking. The first complete translation of the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> from the original languages dates from 1989. Currently, at the level of rural dialects, Galician forms a <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">dialect continuum</a> with Portuguese in the south,<sup id="cite_ref-instituto-camoes1971_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-instituto-camoes1971-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and with <a href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese" class="mw-redirect" title="Astur-Leonese">Astur-Leonese</a> in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez_Rei2011314–387_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESánchez_Rei2011314–387-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mutual_intelligibility" title="Mutual intelligibility">Mutual intelligibility</a> (estimated at 85% by <a href="/wiki/Robert_A._Hall_Jr." title="Robert A. Hall Jr.">Robert A. Hall Jr.</a>, 1989) is very high between Galicians and northern Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-e18_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e18-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Estatuto_de_Galicia_de_1936,_pdf_texto_gl.pdf" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Estatuto_de_Galicia_de_1936%2C_pdf_texto_gl.pdf/page1-170px-Estatuto_de_Galicia_de_1936%2C_pdf_texto_gl.pdf.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="219" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Estatuto_de_Galicia_de_1936%2C_pdf_texto_gl.pdf/page1-255px-Estatuto_de_Galicia_de_1936%2C_pdf_texto_gl.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Estatuto_de_Galicia_de_1936%2C_pdf_texto_gl.pdf/page1-340px-Estatuto_de_Galicia_de_1936%2C_pdf_texto_gl.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1120" data-file-height="1445" /></a><figcaption>Statute of Galicia, 1936</figcaption></figure>
<p>The current linguistic status of Galician with respect to Portuguese is controversial in Galicia, and the issue sometimes carries political overtones. There are <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguists</a> who consider Galician and Portuguese as two <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">norms</a> or varieties of the <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_lyric" title="Galician-Portuguese lyric">same language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESánchez_Rei201124_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESánchez_Rei201124-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Some authors, such as <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Lindley_Cintra" title="Luís Lindley Cintra">Lindley Cintra</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-instituto-camoes1971_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-instituto-camoes1971-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> consider that they are still co-dialects of a <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_lyric" title="Galician-Portuguese lyric">common language</a> in spite of differences in phonology and vocabulary, while others<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> argue that they have become separate languages due to differences in phonetics and vocabulary usage, and, to a lesser extent, morphology and syntax. Fernández Rei in 1990 stated that the Galician language is, with respect to Portuguese, an <a href="/wiki/Ausbausprache,_Abstandsprache_and_Dachsprache" class="mw-redirect" title="Ausbausprache, Abstandsprache and Dachsprache"><i>ausbau</i> language</a>, a language through elaboration, and not an <a href="/wiki/Ausbausprache,_Abstandsprache_and_Dachsprache" class="mw-redirect" title="Ausbausprache, Abstandsprache and Dachsprache"><i>abstand</i> language</a>, a language through detachment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200318_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200318-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With respect to the external and internal perception of this relation, for instance in past editions of the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i>, Galician was defined as a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_dialects" title="Portuguese dialects">"Portuguese dialect"</a> spoken in northwestern Spain. On the other hand, the director of the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Cam%C3%B5es" title="Instituto Camões">Instituto Camões</a> declared in 2019 that Galician and Portuguese were close kin, but different languages.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> According to the Galician government, universities and main cultural institutions, such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_Language_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Galician Language Institute (page does not exist)">Galician Language Institute</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Galician_Academy" title="Royal Galician Academy">Royal Galician Academy</a>, Galician and Portuguese are independent languages that stemmed from medieval Galician-Portuguese,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and modern Galician must be considered an independent <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance language">Romance language</a> belonging to the group of <a href="/wiki/Ibero-Romance" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibero-Romance">Ibero-Romance</a> languages having strong ties with Portuguese and its northern dialects. The standard <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">orthography</a> has its roots in the writing of relatively modern <a href="/wiki/Rexurdimento" title="Rexurdimento">Rexurdimento</a> authors, who largely adapted Spanish orthography to the then mostly unwritten language. Most Galician speakers regard Galician as a separate language,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> which evolved without interruption and in situ from Latin, with Galician and Portuguese maintaining separate literary traditions since the 14th century.
</p><p>Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern Era">Early Modern Era</a> grammars and scholars, at least since Duarte Nunes de Leão in 1606, considered Portuguese and Galician two different languages<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> derived from old Galician, understood as the language spoken in the Northwest before the establishment of the Kingdom of Portugal in the 12th century. The surge of the two languages would be the result of both the elaboration of Portuguese, through the royal court, its internationalization and its study and culture;<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and of the stagnation of Galician.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg/220px-Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg/330px-Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg/440px-Martim_Codax_Cantigas_de_Amigo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1559" data-file-height="1130" /></a><figcaption>Vindel's parchment, containing music and lyrics of several 13th-century <i>cantigas</i> by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Codax" title="Martin Codax">Martin Codax</a></figcaption></figure><p>The earliest internal attestation of the expression <i>Galician language</i> ("lingoajen galego") dates from the 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998142_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998142-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In Spanish "lenguaje gallego" is already documented in this same century, <i>circa</i> 1330;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998144_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998144-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a> <i>circa</i> 1290, in the <i>Regles de Trobar</i> by Catalan author <a href="/wiki/Jofre_de_Foix%C3%A0" title="Jofre de Foixà">Jofre de Foixà</a>: "<i>si tu vols far un cantar en frances, no·s tayn que·y mescles proençal ne cicilia ne </i>gallego<i> ne altre lengatge que sia strayn a aquell</i>" [<i>If you want to compose a song in French, you should not admix Provençal nor Sicilian nor Galician nor other language which is different from it</i>].<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998142_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998142-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reintegrationism_and_political_implications">Reintegrationism and political implications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Reintegrationism and political implications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Private cultural associations, not endorsed by Galician or Portuguese governments, such as the <a href="/wiki/Galician_Language_Association" title="Galician Language Association">Galician Language Association</a> (<i>Associaçom Galega da Língua</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Galician_Academy_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Galician Academy of the Portuguese Language">Galician Academy of the Portuguese Language</a> (<i>Academia Galega da Língua Portuguesa</i>), advocates of the minority <a href="/wiki/Reintegrationist" class="mw-redirect" title="Reintegrationist">Reintegrationist</a> movement, support the idea that differences between Galician and Portuguese speech are not enough to justify considering them as separate languages: Galician would be simply one variety of Galician-Portuguese,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/European_Portuguese" title="European Portuguese">European Portuguese</a>; <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Portuguese" title="Brazilian Portuguese">Brazilian Portuguese</a>; <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese in Africa">African Portuguese</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Fala_language" title="Fala language">Fala</a> language spoken in the northwestern corner of Extremadura (Spain), and other dialects. They have adopted slightly-modified or actual Portuguese orthography, which has its roots in medieval Galician-Portuguese poetry as later adapted by the Portuguese Chancellery.
</p><p>According to Reintegrationists, considering Galician as an independent language reduces contact with Portuguese culture, leaving Galician as a minor language with less capacity to counterbalance the influence of Spanish, the only official language between the 18th century and 1975. On the other hand, viewing Galician as a part of the Lusophony, while not denying its own characteristics (cf. <a href="/wiki/Swiss_German" title="Swiss German">Swiss German</a>), shifts cultural influence from the Spanish domain to the Portuguese. Some scholars<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> have described the situation as properly a continuum, from the Galician variants of Portuguese in one extreme to the Spanish language in the other (which would represent the complete linguistic shift from Galician to Spanish); reintegrationist points of view are closer to the Portuguese extreme, and so-called isolationist ones would be closer to the Spanish one;<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This citation refers to a webpage with a list of scholarly works, which of them is referring to? (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> however, the major Galician nationalist parties, <a href="/wiki/Anova%E2%80%93Nationalist_Brotherhood" class="mw-redirect" title="Anova–Nationalist Brotherhood">Anova–Nationalist Brotherhood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galician_Nationalist_Bloc" title="Galician Nationalist Bloc">Galician Nationalist Bloc</a>, do not use reintegrationist orthographical conventions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_relations_between_Galicia_and_the_Lusophony">Official relations between Galicia and the Lusophony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Official relations between Galicia and the Lusophony"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, the parliament of Galicia unanimously approved Law 1/2014 regarding the promotion of the Portuguese language and links with the <a href="/wiki/Lusophony" class="mw-redirect" title="Lusophony">Lusophony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, on 20 October 2016, the city of <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Compostela" title="Santiago de Compostela">Santiago de Compostela</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>, approved by unanimity a proposal to become an observer member of the Union of Portuguese-Speaking Capitals (<a href="/wiki/Uni%C3%A3o_das_Cidades_Capitais_Luso-Afro-Am%C3%A9rico-Asi%C3%A1ticas" class="mw-redirect" title="União das Cidades Capitais Luso-Afro-Américo-Asiáticas">UCCLA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Also, on 1 November 2016, the Council of Galician Culture (<i>Consello da Cultura Galega</i>, an official institution of defence and promotion of the Galician culture and language) was admitted as a consultative observer of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Speaking Countries</a> (CPLP).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A "friendship and cooperation" protocol was signed between the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Galician_Academy" title="Royal Galician Academy">Royal Galician Academy</a> (RAG) and the <a href="/wiki/Academia_Brasileira_de_Letras" title="Academia Brasileira de Letras">Brazilian Academy of Letters</a> on 10 January 2019. Víctor F. Freixanes, president of the RAG, stated during the ceremony that "there is a conscience that the Galician language is part of a family which includes our brothers from Portugal, Brazil, Angola, Cape Verde, Mozambique... a territory full of possibilities also for Galician. We always said that Galician is not a regional language, but is in fact part of that international project".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution_and_legal_status">Geographic distribution and legal status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution and legal status"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Galician is spoken by some three million people,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> including most of the population of <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and the numerous Galician communities established elsewhere, in Spain (<a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, Barcelona, <a href="/wiki/Biscay" title="Biscay">Biscay</a>), in other European cities (<a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a>, Geneva, London, Paris), and in the Americas (New York, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, Buenos Aires, Córdoba/Argentina, <a href="/wiki/Montevideo" title="Montevideo">Montevideo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, Caracas, <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, São Paulo, <a href="/wiki/Managua" title="Managua">Managua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayagüez">Mayagüez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>, Panama City).
</p><p>Galician is today official, together with the Spanish language, in the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous community">autonomous community</a> of Galicia, where it is recognized as the autochthonous language (<i>lingua propia</i>), being by law the first language of the local administrations and governments. It is supposed by law to be taught bilingually, alongside Spanish, in both primary and secondary education, although the accomplishment of this law is allegedly doubted. It is also used at the three universities established in Galicia, having also the consideration of official language of the three institutions. Galician has also legal recognition in the <a href="/wiki/Bierzo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bierzo">Bierzo</a> region in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Province of León">León</a>, and in four municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Zamora" title="Province of Zamora">Zamora</a>. The other languages with official status elsewhere in Spain are Spanish, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Valencian_language" title="Valencian language">Valencian</a>), <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aranese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Aranese language">Aranese</a>. Galician has also been accepted orally as Portuguese in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, being used by some Galician representatives, among others: <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Posada" title="José Posada">José Posada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Nogueira" class="mw-redirect" title="Camilo Nogueira">Camilo Nogueira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xos%C3%A9_Manuel_Beiras" title="Xosé Manuel Beiras">Xosé Manuel Beiras</a>.
</p><p>Controversy exists regarding the inclusion of <a href="/wiki/Eonavian" class="mw-redirect" title="Eonavian">Eonavian</a> (spoken in the western end of <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a>, bordering <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>) into the Galician language, as it has some traits in common with <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Western Asturian</a> (spoken in the middle west of Asturias). There are those defending these linguistic varieties as <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">dialects of transition</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Astur-Leonese group">Astur-Leonese group</a> on the one hand, and those defending it as clearly Galician varieties on the other (actually both views are compatible).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The recent edition of the cartularies of Oscos in <a href="/wiki/Old_Common_Council_of_Castropol" title="Old Common Council of Castropol">Old Common Council of Castropol</a> and cartularies of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Obona&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Obona (page does not exist)">Obona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornellana" title="Cornellana">Cornellana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corias" title="Corias">Corias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belmonte_de_Miranda" title="Belmonte de Miranda">Belmonte</a> in middle west of Asturias have shown a huge difference in the medieval speech between both banks of the Navia river.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> An examination of the old documents of the Eonavian monastery of Oscos, written from the late 12th to early 14th century to 16th century, shows a clear identification of this language with the Galician-Portuguese linguistic group; while contemporary parchments elsewhere in Asturias are written in Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The two most important traits of those commonly used to tell apart Galician-Portuguese and Asturian-Leonese varieties are the preservation of the mid-open vowels <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ/</span>, which became diphthongs in Asturian-Leonese, and the loss of intervocalic <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>, preserved in the latter language.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200318–23_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200318–23-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ForoBoBurgo.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/ForoBoBurgo.jpg/170px-ForoBoBurgo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="231" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/ForoBoBurgo.jpg/255px-ForoBoBurgo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/ForoBoBurgo.jpg/340px-ForoBoBurgo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2611" /></a><figcaption>One of the oldest legal charters written in Galician, the constitutional charter of the Bo Burgo (Good Burg) of <a href="/wiki/Castro_Caldelas" title="Castro Caldelas">Castro Caldelas</a>, 1228</figcaption></figure>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1206409297">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:250px; ;">
<div class="quotebox-title" style=""><i>Excerpt of medieval Galician poetry (with English translation)</i></div>
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<div class="poem">
<p>Porque no mundo mengou a verdade,<br />
punhei um dia de a ir buscar;<br />
e, u por ela fui nom preguntar,<br />
disserom todos: «Alhur la buscade,<br />
ca de tal guisa se foi a perder,<br />
que nom podemos en novas haver<br />
nem já nom anda na irmaindade.»<br />
<br />
Because in the world the truth has faded,<br />
I decided to go a-searching for it<br />
and wherever I went asking for it<br />
everybody said: 'Search elsewhere<br />
because truth is lost in such a way<br />
such as we can have no news of it<br />
nor is it around here anymore.'
</p>
</div>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="right-aligned" style=""><a href="/wiki/Airas_Nunes" title="Airas Nunes">Airas Nunes</a> (B 871, V 455. 13th century)</cite>
</p>
</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Galician_language" title="History of the Galician language">History of the Galician language</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg/170px-Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="70" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg/255px-Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg/340px-Texto_-_Noia_-_Galiza.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="1443" /></a><figcaption>Mediaeval Galician inscription in a 14th-century house, in <a href="/wiki/Noia" title="Noia">Noia</a>: "ESTAS CASAS MANDOU FAZER VASCO DA COSTA, ERA DE MCCCLXXVII" <i>These houses were ordered by Vasco da Costa, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_era" title="Spanish era">era</a> 1377 (1339 AD)</i></figcaption></figure>
<p>Latinate Galician charters from the 8th century onward show that the local written Latin was heavily influenced by local spoken Romance, yet is not until the 12th century that there is evidence for the identification of the local language as a language different from Latin itself.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> During this same 12th century there are full Galician sentences being inadvertently used inside Latin texts, while its first reckoned use as a literary language dates to the last years of this same century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouto_Cabo2008&#91;&#91;Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2021&#93;&#93;&lt;sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;&#91;&#91;Wikipedia:Citing_sources&#124;&lt;span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2021)&quot;&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;&#93;&#93;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouto_Cabo2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2021]]&lt;sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2021)&quot;&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQueixas_Zas200114_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQueixas_Zas200114-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The linguistic stage from the 13th to the 15th centuries is usually known as Galician-Portuguese (or <i>Old Portuguese</i>, or <i>Old Galician</i>) as an acknowledgement of the cultural and linguistic unity of Galicia and Portugal during the Middle Ages, as the two linguistic varieties differed only in dialectal minor phenomena.
</p><p>This language flourished during the 13th and 14th centuries as a language of culture, developing <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese_lyric" title="Galician-Portuguese lyric">a rich lyric tradition</a> of which some 2000 compositions (<i><a href="/wiki/Cantigas" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantigas">cantigas</a></i>, meaning 'songs') have been preserved—a few hundred even with their musical score—in a series of collections, and belonging to four main genres: <b>cantigas de amor</b>, love songs, where a man sings for his ladylove; <i><a href="/wiki/Cantiga_de_amigo" title="Cantiga de amigo">cantigas de amigo</a></i>, where a woman sings for her boyfriend; <b>cantigas de escarnio</b>, crude, taunting, and sexual songs of scorn; <b>cantigas de maldecir</b>, where the poet vents his spleen openly; and also the <a href="/wiki/Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria" title="Cantigas de Santa Maria">Cantigas de Santa María</a>, which are religious songs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQueixas_Zas200124–61_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQueixas_Zas200124–61-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The oldest known document is the poem <i>Ora faz ost'o Senhor de Navarra</i> by Joam Soares de Paiva, written around 1200. The first non-literary documents in Galician-Portuguese date from the early 13th century, the Noticia de Torto (1211) and the Testamento of <a href="/wiki/Afonso_II_of_Portugal" title="Afonso II of Portugal">Afonso II of Portugal</a> (1214), both samples of medieval notarial prose.
</p><p>Its most notable patrons—themselves reputed authors—were king <a href="/wiki/Dom_Dinis" class="mw-redirect" title="Dom Dinis">Dom Dinis</a> in Portugal, and king <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X_of_Castile" title="Alfonso X of Castile">Alfonso X the Learned</a> in Galicia, Castile and León, who was a great promoter of both Galician and <a href="/wiki/Castilian_Spanish" title="Castilian Spanish">Castilian Spanish</a> languages. Not just the kings encouraged literary creation in Galician-Portuguese, but also the noble houses of Galicia and Portugal, as being an author or bringing reputed troubadours into one's home became a way of promoting social prestige; as a result many noblemen, businessmen and clergymen of the 13th and 14th centuries became notable authors, such as Paio Gomes Charinho, lord of <a href="/wiki/Rianxo" title="Rianxo">Rianxo</a>, and the aforementioned kings.
</p><p>Aside from the lyric genres, Galicia developed also a minor tradition on literary prose, most notably in translation of European popular series, as those dealing with <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur" title="King Arthur">King Arthur</a> written by <a href="/wiki/Chretien_de_Troyes" class="mw-redirect" title="Chretien de Troyes">Chretien de Troyes</a>, or those based on the <a href="/wiki/Roman_de_Troie" title="Roman de Troie">war of Troy</a>, usually paid and commissioned by noblemen who desired to read those romances in their own language. Other genres include history books (either translation of Spanish ones, or original creations like the <i>Chronicle of St. Mary of Iria</i>, by Rui Vasques), religious books, legal studies, and a treaty on horse breeding.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Most prose literary creation in Galician had stopped by the 16th century, when <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">printing press</a> became popular; the first complete translation of the Bible was not printed until the 20th century.
</p><p>As for other written uses of Galician, legal charters (last wills, hirings, sales, constitutional charters, city council book of acts, guild constitutions, books of possessions, and any type of public or private contracts and inventories) written in Galicia are to be found from 1230 to 1530—the earliest one probably a document from the monastery of <a href="/wiki/Mel%C3%B3n" title="Melón">Melón</a>, dated in 1231<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouto_Cabo200851_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouto_Cabo200851-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>—being Galician by far the most used language during the 13th, 14th and 15th centuries, in substitution of Latin.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diglossia_and_influence_of_the_Spanish_language">Diglossia and influence of the Spanish language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Diglossia and influence of the Spanish language"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1134653256">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9;display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096940132">.mw-parser-output .listen .side-box-text{line-height:1.1em}.mw-parser-output .listen-plain{border:none;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded{width:100%;margin:0;border-width:1px 0 0 0;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-header{padding:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded .listen-header{padding:2px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen-file-header{padding:4px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen .description{padding-top:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen .mw-tmh-player{max-width:100%}@media(max-width:719px){.mw-parser-output .listen{clear:both}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .listen:not(.listen-noimage){width:320px}.mw-parser-output .listen-left{overflow:visible;float:left}.mw-parser-output .listen-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style>
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></span><figcaption></figcaption></figure></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Maria.ogg" title="File:Santa Maria.ogg">"Santa Maria, strela do dia"</a></div>
<div><span typeof="mw:File"><span><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="232" style="width:232px;" data-durationhint="151" data-mwtitle="Santa_Maria.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/1/13/Santa_Maria.ogg/Santa_Maria.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Santa_Maria.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-width="0" data-height="0" /></audio></span></span></div>
<div class="description">A 13th-century Galician-Portuguese <i>Cantiga</i></div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<p>Galician-Portuguese lost its political unity when the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a> obtained its independence from the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">Kingdom of León</a>, a transition initiated in 1139 and completed in 1179, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a>. Meanwhile, the Kingdom of Galicia was united with the Kingdom of León, and later with the Kingdom of Castile, under kings of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burgundy" title="House of Burgundy">House of Burgundy</a>. The Galician and Portuguese standards of the language diverged over time, following independent evolutionary paths. Portuguese was the official language of the Portuguese chancellery, while Galician was the usual language not only of troubadours and peasants, but also of local noblemen and clergy, and of their officials, so forging and maintaining two slightly different standards.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg/170px-13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg/255px-13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg/340px-13th-century_unknown_painters_-_Cantigas_de_Alfonso_el_Sabio_-_WGA16031.jpg 2x" data-file-width="598" data-file-height="840" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Cantigas_de_Santa_Maria" title="Cantigas de Santa Maria">Cantigas de Santa Maria</a>, 13th century</figcaption></figure>
<p>During the reign of <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfonso X">Alfonso X</a>, Spanish became the official language of the chancellery of the Kingdom of Castile. However, in Galicia and neighboring regions of Asturias and León in 1200–1500, the local languages remained the usual written languages in any type of document, either legal or narrative, public or private. Spanish was progressively introduced through Royal decrees and the edicts of foreign churchmen and officials. This led, from the late 15th century on, to the end of legal documents in Galician; the last ones were issued around 1530.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998188–193_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998188–193-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Also, from 1480 on, notaries of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a> were required to obtain their licenses in <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a>, where they had to prove their mastery of Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998188–193_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998188–193-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg/220px-Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg/330px-Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg/440px-Galician_Johan_Tuorum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>14th-century inscription, in Galician language: 'ESTA&#160;: IMAGEE&#160;: HE&#160;: AQVI&#160;: POSTA&#160;: POR: ALMA&#160;: D(E)&#160;: I(O)HA(N)&#160;: TVORUM' 'This image is here in exposition for the soul of Joham Tuorum'.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In spite of Galician being the most spoken language, during the 17th century the elites of the Kingdom began speaking Spanish, most notably in towns and cities. The linguistic situation in Galicia became one of <a href="/wiki/Diglossia" title="Diglossia">diglossia</a>, with Galician as the low variety and Spanish as the high one.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In reaction to the relegation of the autochthonous language, a series of literary and historical works (always written in Spanish) appeared in the 17th century through 19th century, meant to vindicate the history, language, people, and culture of Galicia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998235–265_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998235–265-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The period from the 16th century to the early 19th century, when Galician had little literary—and no legal—use, is considered the dark age of Galician language. The Galician spoken and written then is usually referred to as <i>Middle Galician</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Galician">Middle Galician</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Middle Galician"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg/170px-Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg" decoding="async" width="170" height="247" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg/255px-Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg/340px-Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="696" data-file-height="1013" /></a><figcaption>Martín Sarmiento</figcaption></figure>
<p>Middle Galician is known mostly through popular literature (songs, carols, proverbs, theatrical scripts, personal letters), but also through the frequent apparition of Galician interferences and personal and place names in local works and documents otherwise written in Spanish. Other important sources are a number of <a href="/wiki/Sonnet" title="Sonnet">sonnets</a> and other lyric poetry, as well as other literate productions, including the forgery of allegedly mediaeval scriptures or chronicles under diverse pretensions—usually to show the ancient nobility of the forger's family—being these writings elaborated in an archaic looking Galician which nevertheless could not conceal the state of the language during this period.
</p><p>Middle Galician is characterized by a series of phonetic processes which led to a further separation from Portuguese, and to the apparition of some of the more noteworthy dialectal features, among other phenomenons: emergence of the <i>gheada</i> or pronunciation of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> as a pharyngeal fricative; denasalization of nasal vowels in most of Galicia, becoming oral vowels in the east, or a group formed by an oral vowel plus a nasal consonant in the west; reduction of the sibilant system, with the confluence (except in the <i>Baixa Limia</i> region) of voiced and voiceless fricatives, followed by a process of de-affrication which led to different results in the west and in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998265–288_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMariño_Paz1998265–288-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most important author during this period of the language was the scholar <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Sarmiento" title="Martín Sarmiento">Martín Sarmiento</a>, unconditional defender and the first researcher of Galician language (history, evolution, lexicon, etymology, onomastics). His <i>Elementos etimológicos segun el método de Euclides</i> (1766), written in Spanish but dealing with Galician, was in fact one of the first comprehensive studies on sound change and evolution of any European language. He also defended that teaching in Galicia should be conducted in Galician, since it was the common language of most people.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Rexurdimento_.28Renaissance.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rexurdimento_(Renaissance)">Rexurdimento (Renaissance)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rexurdimento (Renaissance)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Eduardopondal.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Eduardopondal.jpg/170px-Eduardopondal.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="265" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Eduardopondal.jpg/255px-Eduardopondal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Eduardopondal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="467" /></a><figcaption>The 19th-century author <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Pondal" title="Eduardo Pondal">Eduardo Pondal</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>During the 19th century a thriving literature developed, in what was called the <i>Rexurdimento</i> (Resurgence), of the Galician language.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGómez_SánchezQueixas_Zas200193–166_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGómez_SánchezQueixas_Zas200193–166-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> It was headed by three main authors: <a href="/wiki/Rosalia_de_Castro" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosalia de Castro">Rosalia de Castro</a>, an intimist poet; <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Pondal" title="Eduardo Pondal">Eduardo Pondal</a>, of nationalist ideology, who championed a Celtic revival; and <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Curros_Enr%C3%ADquez" title="Manuel Curros Enríquez">Manuel Curros Enríquez</a>, a liberal and anticlerical author whose ideas and proclamations were scandalous for part of the 19th-century society.
</p><p>The first political manifest asking for the officialization of Galician date to the late 19th century.
</p><p>An important landmarks was the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Galician_Academy" title="Royal Galician Academy">Royal Galician Academy</a>, in 1906, soon followed by that of the <a href="/wiki/Seminario_de_Estudos_Galegos" title="Seminario de Estudos Galegos">Seminario de Estudos Galegos</a> (1923). The <i>Seminario</i> was devoted to the research and study of the Galician culture. It was created by a group of students: <a href="/wiki/Ferm%C3%ADn_Bouza_Brey" title="Fermín Bouza Brey">Fermín Bouza Brey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xos%C3%A9_Filgueira_Valverde" title="Xosé Filgueira Valverde">Xosé Filgueira Valverde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lois_Tob%C3%ADo_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Lois Tobío Fernández">Lois Tobío Fernández</a>, with the collaboration of <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Carvalho_Calero" class="mw-redirect" title="Ricardo Carvalho Calero">Ricardo Carvalho Calero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3n_Fraguas" title="Antón Fraguas">Antón Fraguas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xaqu%C3%ADn_Lorenzo_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Xaquín Lorenzo Fernández">Xaquín Lorenzo Fernández</a>.
</p><p>Following the victory of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, the written or public use of the Galician language was outlawed.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_(2001_vs_2011).png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%282001_vs_2011%29.png/220px-Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%282001_vs_2011%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%282001_vs_2011%29.png/330px-Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%282001_vs_2011%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%282001_vs_2011%29.png/440px-Percentage_of_Galician_speakers_%282001_vs_2011%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1692" data-file-height="1054" /></a><figcaption>Speakers of Galician as a first language in 2001 and 2011, according to the Galician Institute of Statistics</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/220px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="194" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/330px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG/440px-Galician_linguistic_areas.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1485" data-file-height="1308" /></a><figcaption>Galician linguistic areas</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Galizaestremeira.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Galizaestremeira.png/220px-Galizaestremeira.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="214" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Galizaestremeira.png/330px-Galizaestremeira.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Galizaestremeira.png/440px-Galizaestremeira.png 2x" data-file-width="641" data-file-height="624" /></a><figcaption>Galician-speaking areas outside Galicia (yellow)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Publishing of Galician-language material revived on a small scale in the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinahan2000279–281_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinahan2000279–281-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Galician_language_today">The Galician language today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The Galician language today"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the advent of democracy, Galician has been brought into the country's institutions, and it is now co-official with Spanish in Galicia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinahan2000279–281_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinahan2000279–281-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Galician is taught in schools, and there is a public Galician-language television channel, <a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3n_de_Galicia" title="Televisión de Galicia">Televisión de Galicia</a>.
</p><p>Today, the most common language for everyday use in the largest cities of Galicia is Spanish rather than Galician, as a result of this long process of <a href="/wiki/Language_shift" title="Language shift">language shift</a>. However, Galician is still the main language in rural areas.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Galician_Academy" title="Royal Galician Academy">Royal Galician Academy</a> and other Galician institutions celebrate each 17 May as <a href="/wiki/Galician_Literature_Day" title="Galician Literature Day">Galician Literature Day</a> (<span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">Día das Letras Galegas</i></span>), dedicated each year to a deceased Galician-language writer chosen by the academy.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_the_Galician_language">Use of the Galician language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Use of the Galician language"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Use of Galician splits by age, with over half of those over 45 indicating that Galician is their primary language, with lower numbers for the younger population. Those under 45 were more likely than those over 45 to answer that they never use Galician.
</p>
<table style="float: center; border: 1px #AAA solid; border-collapse: collapse; background-color: #E4E4E4; text-align: right;" border="1">

<p>Use of Galician also varies greatly depending on the regions and municipalities of Galicia. While in two areas of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Province of A Coruña">Province of A Coruña</a> (<a href="/wiki/Costa_da_Morte" title="Costa da Morte">Costa da Morte</a> and the Southeast) more than 90% of the population always or mostly speaks in Galician, only the 15,2% of the population does the same in the city of <a href="/wiki/Vigo" title="Vigo">Vigo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
