<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Dialects"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some authors are of the opinion that Galician possesses no real dialects.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, Galician local varieties are collected in three main <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialectal</a> blocks, each block comprising a series of areas, being local linguistic varieties that are all <a href="/wiki/Mutually_intelligible" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutually intelligible">mutually intelligible</a>. Some of the main features which distinguish the three blocks are:
</p>
<ul><li>The resolution of medieval <a href="/wiki/Nasalized_vowels" class="mw-redirect" title="Nasalized vowels">nasalized vowels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hiatus (linguistics)">hiatus</a>: these sometimes turned into <a href="/wiki/Diphthongs" class="mw-redirect" title="Diphthongs">diphthongs</a> in the east, while in the center and west the vowels in the hiatus were sometimes assimilated. Later, in the eastern—except Ancarese Galician—and central blocks, the nasal trait was lost, while in the west the nasal trait usually developed into an implosive nasal consonant <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="implosive usually means a consonant articulated with ingressive airflow, and it is, to my knowledge, always a stop consonant. What is meant by implosive here? (December 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerreiro1999132_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerreiro1999132-61">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200358_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200358-62">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In general, these led to important dialectal variability in the inflection in genre and number of words ended in a nasal consonant. So, from medieval <i>irmão</i> 'brother', <i>ladrões</i> 'robbers', <i>irmãas</i> 'sisters' developed eastern Galician <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">irmao</i></span>, <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">ladrois</i></span>, <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">irmás</i></span>; central Galician <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">irmao</i></span>, <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">ladrós</i></span>, <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">irmás</i></span>; western Galician <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">irmán</i></span>, <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">ladróns</i></span>, <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">irmáns</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200359–67_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200359–67-63">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<dl><dd>An exception to this rule is constituted by the hiatus in which the first vowel was a nasalized i or u. In those cases, a nasal, palatal <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲ/</span> or velar <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span> was usually inserted: <i>ũa</i> 'a / one (fem.)' &gt; <i>unha</i> (Portuguese <i>uma</i>), -<i>ina</i> &gt; -<i>ĩa</i> &gt; -<i>iña</i> (Portuguese -<i>inha</i>). Nevertheless, in Ancarese and Asturian Galician, this process did not take place: A-G <i>vecía</i>, Ancarese <i>vecĩa</i> vs. standard <i>veciña</i> '(female) neighbor' (Port. <i>vizinha</i>), A-G <i>úa</i>, Ancarese <i>ũa</i> vs. standard <i>unha</i> (Port. uma).</dd></dl>
<ul><li>The resolution of hiatus formed by oral vowels had similar developments, most notably those derived from the loss of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l/</span>, which again had important consequences for the declension of words ending in <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l/</span>. So, Medieval Galician <span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">animaes</i></span> 'animals' (sing. <i>animal</i>); central and western Galician <i>animás</i>; eastern Galician <i>animais</i>; Asturian Galician <i>animales</i> (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l/</span> is preserved).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200364–65_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200364–65-64">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the west, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> is rendered as a fricative <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">x</a><span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span><a href="/wiki/Voiceless_pharyngeal_fricative" title="Voiceless pharyngeal fricative">ħ</a><span class="wrap"> </span>~<span class="wrap"> </span><a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">h</a>]</span> (<i><a href="/wiki/Gheada" title="Gheada">gheada</a></i>), except after a nasal, where it can become a stop <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_plosive" title="Voiceless velar plosive">k</a>&#93;</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei2003163–189_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei2003163–189-65">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Stressed vowel <a href="/wiki/Metaphony_(Romance_languages)" title="Metaphony (Romance languages)">metaphony</a> is most notable in the west and center, while in the east it is unknown. It is triggered by a final <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span>, which tends to close <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_vowel" title="Open-mid vowel">open-mid vowels</a>, or by a final <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> which tends to open <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_vowel" title="Close-mid vowel">close-mid</a> ones.</li>
<li>There are three main <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">sibilant</a> systems, all derived from the medieval Galician one, which was richer and more complex:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei2003213_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei2003213-66">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li>The common one, extended in the eastern and center regions, presents an opposition <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/<span class="wrap"> </span>–<span class="wrap"> </span>/s/<span class="wrap"> </span>–<span class="wrap"> </span>/θ/</span>. In the westernmost parts of this area the opposition of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/θ/</span> is lost in postnuclear position, in the coda, both being produced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span>.</li>
<li>In the coastal western areas the opposition is <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/<span class="wrap"> </span>–<span class="wrap"> </span>/s/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> being produced in some regions as a laminal or in some others as an apical. Sometimes this system is even further reduced to just a single <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span>. On the other hand, in some areas final <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> is produced as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span>, as in plenty of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_dialects" title="Portuguese dialects">Portuguese dialects</a>.</li>
<li>In the Limia Baixa region an old six sibilant system is still preserved, with voiced/voiceless opposition: <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/<span class="wrap"> </span>–<span class="wrap"> </span>/ʒ/</span>; <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s̺/<span class="wrap"> </span>–<span class="wrap"> </span>/z̺/</span> (apical) and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s̻/<span class="wrap"> </span>–<span class="wrap"> </span>/z̻/</span> (laminal).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200357_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFernández_Rei200357-67">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul>
<p>Each dialectal area is then further defined by these and other more restricted traits or isoglosses:
</p>
<ul><li><b>Eastern Galician</b>: Asturian area (<a href="/wiki/Eonavian" class="mw-redirect" title="Eonavian">Eonavian</a>), Ancares area, Zamora area and Central-Eastern area.</li>
<li><b>Central Galician</b>: Mindoniense area, Lucu-auriense area, Central Transitional area, and Eastern Transitional area.</li>
<li><b>Western Galician</b>: Bergantiños area, Fisterra area, Pontevedra area and Lower Limia area.</li></ul>
<p>Standard Galician is usually based on Central Galician characteristics, but it also incorporates western and eastern traits and features.
</p>

<td>you sang
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2"><span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">animás</i></span></td>
<td><b><span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">animais</i></span></b></td>
<td><span title="Galician-language text"><i lang="gl">animaes</i></span></td>

<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_id1"><b><a href="#ref_id1">^</a></b></span>  <a href="/wiki/Metaphony_(Romance_languages)" title="Metaphony (Romance languages)">Metaphony</a> produced by final <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> and by final <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> (usually produced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʊ]</span>). All the diverse productions are considered admissible. In the east there's little to no metaphony.</dd>
<dd><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_id2"><b><a href="#ref_id2">^</a></b></span>  Different evolution of the group <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ste/</span> led to different <a href="/wiki/Desinence" class="mw-redirect" title="Desinence">desinences</a> for the past tense formation along Galician geography.</dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Galician_phonology" title="Galician phonology">Galician phonology</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Galician allows pronominal <a href="/wiki/Clitic" title="Clitic">clitics</a> to be attached to indicative and subjunctive forms, as does Portuguese, unlike modern Spanish. After many centuries of close contact between the two languages, Galician has also adopted many loan words from Spanish, and some <a href="/wiki/Calques" class="mw-redirect" title="Calques">calques</a> of Spanish syntax.
</p><p>Galician usually makes the difference according to gender and categorizes words as masculine "o rapaz" (the young man) or feminine "a rapaza" (the young woman). This difference is present in the articles "o / a / os / as" (the), nouns "o can / a cadela" (the dog / the (female) dog), pronouns "el / ela", (he / she) and adjectives "bonitiño / bonitiña" (pretty, beautiful). There is also a neuter set of demonstrative pronouns "isto, iso, aquilo" (this / that). The most typical ending for masculine words is -o, whereas the most typical ending for feminine is -a "o prato / a tixola" (the plate / the frying pan). The difference in the grammatical gender of a word may correspond to a real gender difference in the physical world "xuicioso / xuiciosa" (sensible); the former adjective will qualify a male, and the latter, a female. However, there is no particular reason for objects to be ascribed to a particular grammatical gender or another, it has to do with the gender having been ascribed by tradition and the use of speakers as in the following examples: "o xis / o samba / a mesa / a caricatura" (chalk / the samba / the table / the caricature).
</p><p>Galician expresses the difference in number with a form for the singular and another for the plural. The most typical suffix to express a plural number is "s", "cantiga / cantigas".
</p><p>There are two different ways of addressing people: one is the most usual informal pronoun "ti" for the second person singular and "vos" for the second person plural. There are formal ways of addressing directly people "vostede" for the singular and "vostedes" for the plural.
</p><p>The last review of the official grammar has established that, if there is no risk of confusion, the exclamation and question marks will appear only at the end of the sentence, thus deprecating the general use of Spanish-like <a href="/wiki/Inverted_question_and_exclamation_marks" title="Inverted question and exclamation marks">inverted question and exclamation marks</a>.
</p><p>The verb is inflected. There are regular and irregular verbs in the language. All verbs will appear listed by means of their infinitive form in dictionaries, and there are three typical endings for verbs "-ar / -er / -ir".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">Orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Galician_alphabet" title="Galician alphabet">Galician alphabet</a></div>
<p>The current official Galician orthography is guided by the "Normas ortográficas e morfolóxicas do Idioma Galego" (NOMIGa),<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> first introduced in 1982, by the Royal Galician Academy (RAG), based on a report by the Instituto da Lingua Galega (ILG). These norms were not accepted by some sectors desiring a norm closer to modern Portuguese (see <a href="/wiki/Reintegrationism" title="Reintegrationism">reintegrationism</a>). In July 2003, the Royal Galician Academy modified the language normative to admit and promote some archaic Galician-Portuguese forms conserved in modern Portuguese, merging the NOMIG and the main proposals of the moderate sectors of reintegrationism; the resulting orthography is used by the vast majority of media, cultural production and virtually all official matters including education.
</p><p>The reintegrationist movement opts for the use of writing systems that range from adapted to whole <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acute_accent">Acute accent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Acute accent"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Syllabic_stress" class="mw-redirect" title="Syllabic stress">Syllabic stress</a> is significant in Galician. One syllable in each word receives primary stress. The syllable receiving the primary stress can generally be identified by the spelling of the word according to the language's rules of orthography. In cases where the stress is not at the default location indicated by the spelling, an <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">acute accent</a> (´) is placed over the main vowel of the stressed syllable, as in <i>paspalhás</i> or <i>paspallás</i> ('quail'), <i>móbil</i> ('mobile'), and <i>cárcere</i> ('jail', 'gaol').
</p><p>The acute accent has some other functions. Sometimes it shows that adjacent vowels represent separate syllables rather than a diphthong. Acute accents are written on top of upper- as well as lower-case letters: <i>Óscar</i>. An acute accent may also be used to distinguish between two words that are otherwise <a href="/wiki/Homonym" title="Homonym">homonyms</a>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-instituto-camoes1971-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-instituto-camoes1971_11-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-instituto-camoes1971_11-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFLindley1971" class="citation cs2 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source">Lindley, Luís F. (1971), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20061102180041/http://www.instituto-camoes.pt/cvc/hlp/biblioteca/novaproposta.pdf">"Nova Proposta de Classificação dos Dialectos Galego-Portugueses"</a> &#91;New Proposal for the Classification of Galician-Portuguese Dialects&#93; <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, <i>Boletim de Filologia, Lisboa, Centro de Estudos Filológicos</i> (in Portuguese), archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.instituto-camoes.pt/cvc/hlp/biblioteca/novaproposta.pdf">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 2 November 2006</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Boletim+de+Filologia%2C+Lisboa%2C+Centro+de+Estudos+Filol%C3%B3gicos&amp;rft.atitle=Nova+Proposta+de+Classifica%C3%A7%C3%A3o+dos+Dialectos+Galego-Portugueses&amp;rft.date=1971&amp;rft.aulast=Lindley&amp;rft.aufirst=Lu%C3%ADs+F.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.instituto-camoes.pt%2Fcvc%2Fhlp%2Fbiblioteca%2Fnovaproposta.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGalician+language" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFFernández_Rei2003">Fernández Rei 2003</a>, p.&#160;17. "Today, from a point of view which is exclusively linguistic, both banks of the Minho river speak the same language, since the Minhoto and Trás-os-Montes dialects are a continuation of the Galician varieties, sharing common traits that differentiate them from the dialect of Central and Southern Portugal; but at the level of the common language, and in a sociolinguistic perspective, in the west of the peninsula there are two modern languages, with differences in pronunciation, morphosyntax and vocabulary", ["Na actualidade, desde o ponto de vista estrictamente lingüístico, ás dúas marxes do Miño fálase o mesmo idioma, pois os dialectos miñotos e trasmontanos son unha continuación dos falares galegos, cos que comparten trazos comúns que os diferencian dos do centro e sur de Portugal; pero no plano da lingua común, e desde unha perspectiva sociolingüística, hai no occidente peninsular dúas línguas modernas, con diferencias fonéticas, morfosintácticas e léxicas"].</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://alpi.csic.es/sites/default/files/PhotoSwipe/images/Atlas_Pag18.jpg">Answers to the question "Name of the local language?"</a> in the <i>Atlas Lingüístico de la Península Ibérica</i>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFRecalde1997" class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source">Recalde, Montserrat (1997). <i>La vitalidad etnolingüística gallega</i> &#91;<i>Galician ethnolinguistic vitality</i>&#93; (in Spanish). València: Centro de Estudios sobre Comunicación Interlingüistíca e Intercultural. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9788437028958" title="Special:BookSources/9788437028958"><bdi>9788437028958</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=La+vitalidad+etnoling%C3%BC%C3%ADstica+gallega&amp;rft.place=Val%C3%A8ncia&amp;rft.pub=Centro+de+Estudios+sobre+Comunicaci%C3%B3n+Interling%C3%BCist%C3%ADca+e+Intercultural&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft.isbn=9788437028958&amp;rft.aulast=Recalde&amp;rft.aufirst=Montserrat&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGalician+language" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Os diphtongos são estes ão ẽe ij õo ũu. que temos comũs cõ os Gallegos, cuja lingoa &amp; a nossa era toda quasi hũa." (the diphthongs are these ... which we have in common with the Galicians, whose language and ours was almost one).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Da qual lingoa Gallega a Portuguesa se aventajou tanto, quãto &amp; na elegãcia della vemos. O que se causou por em Portugal haver Reis, &amp; corte que he a officina onde os vocabulos se forjaõ, &amp; pulem, &amp; donde manão pera os outros homẽs, o que nunqua honve[sic] em Galliza." (From that Galician language the Portuguese got ahead as far as now we see in its elegance. This was caused because of Portugal having Kings, and a Royal court which is the office where words are forged and polished, and from where they flow to the other people; which Galicia never had.)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"por todos estes motivos a alterar-se e distinguir-se a nossa Lingua da Galega, que permaneceo, sem alteração nem melhoramento, encantonada em hum Paiz, sem Côrte, e sem Universidade" (because all of these causes our language changed and distinguished from the Galician one, which remained, with no alterarion or improbement, in the country, with no court or study.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFD’Andrés2019" class="citation journal cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source">D’Andrés, Ramón (2019). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://revistas.ucm.es/index.php/MADR/article/view/66851">"Atlas lingüístico ETLEN sobre la frontera entre el gallegoportugués y el asturleonés en Asturias"</a> &#91;ETLEN, a Linguistic Atlas of the Boundary between Galician-Portuguese and Asturleonese in Asturias (Spain)&#93;. <i>Madrygal. Revista de Estudios Gallegos</i> (in Spanish). <b>22</b>: 51–62. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.5209%2Fmadr.66851">10.5209/madr.66851</a></span>. <a href="/wiki/Hdl_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hdl (identifier)">hdl</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://hdl.handle.net/10651%2F55180">10651/55180</a></span>. <a href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:213657213">213657213</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Madrygal.+Revista+de+Estudios+Gallegos&amp;rft.atitle=Atlas+ling%C3%BC%C3%ADstico+ETLEN+sobre+la+frontera+entre+el+gallegoportugu%C3%A9s+y+el+asturleon%C3%A9s+en+Asturias&amp;rft.volume=22&amp;rft.pages=51-62&amp;rft.date=2019&amp;rft_id=info%3Ahdl%2F10651%2F55180&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A213657213%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.5209%2Fmadr.66851&amp;rft.aulast=D%E2%80%99Andr%C3%A9s&amp;rft.aufirst=Ram%C3%B3n&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Frevistas.ucm.es%2Findex.php%2FMADR%2Farticle%2Fview%2F66851&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGalician+language" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFDamaso_Alonso_Obras1971" class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source">Damaso Alonso Obras (1971). <i>Obras Completas</i>. Volume I: Estudios lingüísticos peninsulares (in Spanish). Gredos. p.&#160;391. <q>Like a rainbow between two close colours, there is a moment, in the way of the West, when we get to feel us into the Galician area, and another side, to the East, in which we get to feel us into Asturian, but there is also a mixed zone, in which, after all, the distinction depends on our way to appreciate and read will depend on a serial linguistics facts. Some another time, I will deal with this question. <b>It is enough saying today that the oldest statement about Galician extending into Asturias up to the Navia River, (Menéndez Pidal, 'El dialecto leonés', §&#160;1, 2, 1906) cannot be more right,</b> in spite of typical linguistic Asturian features crossing to the west over that border. These dialects between the rivers Navia and Eo, mainly Galician, but with clear Asturian features, are what we call 'Gallego-Asturiano'.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Obras+Completas&amp;rft.series=Volume+I%3A+Estudios+ling%C3%BC%C3%ADsticos+peninsulares&amp;rft.pages=391&amp;rft.pub=Gredos&amp;rft.date=1971&amp;rft.au=Damaso+Alonso+Obras&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGalician+language" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>

Vol.&#160;5. pp.&#160;181–203 &#8211; via Hemeroteca Digital (Biblioteca Nacional de España).</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Revista+ib%C3%A9rica+de+ciencias%2C+pol%C3%ADtica%2C+literatura%2C+artes+e+instrucci%C3%B3n+p%C3%BAblica&amp;rft.atitle=O+dialecto+asturiano&amp;rft.volume=5&amp;rft.pages=181-203&amp;rft.date=1862&amp;rft.aulast=Laverde+y+Ruiz&amp;rft.aufirst=Gumersindo&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fhemerotecadigital.bne.es%2Fissue.vm%3Fid%3D0003775992%26search%3D%26lang%3Den&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGalician+language" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As an example, in a passage of the <a href="/wiki/Historia_Compostellana" class="mw-redirect" title="Historia Compostellana">Historia Compostellana</a> it is stated, as a notable event, that bishop Diego Gelmirez spoke publicly in Latin.</span>

<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://buscon.rae.es/draei/srvltobtenerhtml?lema=can&amp;supind=1&amp;carext=10000&amp;nedic=no">"real academia española"</a>. buscon.rae.es<span class="reference-accessdate">. <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Galician_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Further reading"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFCastro2013" class="citation journal cs1">Castro, Olga (February 2013). "Talking at cross-purposes? The missing link between feminist linguistics and translation studies". <i><a href="/wiki/Gender_and_Language" title="Gender and Language">Gender and Language</a></i>. <b>7</b> (1): 35–58. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1558%2Fgenl.v7i1.35">10.1558/genl.v7i1.35</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Gender+and+Language&amp;rft.atitle=Talking+at+cross-purposes%3F+The+missing+link+between+feminist+linguistics+and+translation+studies&amp;rft.volume=7&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=35-58&amp;rft.date=2013-02&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1558%2Fgenl.v7i1.35&amp;rft.aulast=Castro&amp;rft.aufirst=Olga&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGalician+language" class="Z3988"></span> Examines the arguments for and against the use of inclusive language in (literary) translation through an analysis of the "ideological struggle" that emerged from two ideologically disparate rewritings of gender markers into Galician of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Curious_Incident_of_the_Dog_in_the_Night-Time" title="The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night-Time">The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night-Time</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Haddon" title="Mark Haddon">Mark Haddon</a> (2003), focusing on the ideological, poetic and economic pressures that (still) define the professional practice of translation.</li></ul>

</p>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ilg.usc.es/ago/">Arquivo do Galego Oral</a> – An archive of records of Galician speakers.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://consellodacultura.org/arquivos/asg/anosafala.php">A Nosa Fala</a> – Sound recordings of the different dialects of the Galician language.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080930002413/http://www.agal-gz.org/modules.php?name=Sections&amp;op=viewarticle&amp;artid=15">Amostra comparativa</a> – Comparison between Galician, Portuguese and Brazilian-Portuguese pronunciation (with sound files) (reintegrationist Galician)</li></ul>
<p>Corpora:
</p>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ilg.usc.es/tmilg/index.php">Tesouro medieval informatizado da lingua galega</a>. <span class="languageicon">(in Galician)</span></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sli.uvigo.es/xelmirez/">Corpus Xelmirez</a> – A corpus on medieval Galician documentation, in Galician, Latin, and Spanish.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ilg.usc.es/TILG/?lng=en">Tesouro informatizado da lingua galega</a>. <span class="languageicon">(in English and Galician)</span></li></ul>
<p>Dictionaries:
</p>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.realacademiagalega.org/dicionario">Royal Galician Academy Dictionary</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130722230111/http://www.realacademiagalega.org/dicionario">Archived</a> 22 July 2013 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> <span class="languageicon">(in Galician)</span></li>
<li><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Appendix:Galician_pronouns" class="extiw" title="wikt:Appendix:Galician pronouns">Appendix:Galician pronouns</a> – on Wiktionary</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sli.uvigo.es/CLIG/index_en.html">English-Galician CLUVI Online Dictionary</a> (official Galician)</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20040410195531/http://www.websters-online-dictionary.org/definition/Galician-english/">Galician – English Dictionary</a>: from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120223164907/http://www.websters-online-dictionary.org/">Webster's Online Dictionary</a> – <a href="/wiki/The_Rosetta_Edition" class="mw-redirect" title="The Rosetta Edition">The Rosetta Edition</a>. (Official Galician),</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://valesne.homestead.com/untitled11.html">A short English-Galician-Japanese Phraselist (Renewal)</a> incl. sound soft (Official Galician), <span class="languageicon">(in English and Japanese)</span></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sli.uvigo.es/DDGM/">Dicionario de dicionarios do galego medieval</a> – A dictionary of Old Galician dictionaries. <span class="languageicon">(in Galician)</span></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sli.uvigo.es/ddd/index.html">Dicionario de dicionarios</a> – A dictionary of Galician dictionaries. <span class="languageicon">(in Galician)</span></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.estraviz.org/">e-Estraviz</a> – Isaac Alonso Estraviz's dictionary (on-line). (reintegrationist norm and official norm)</li></ul>

<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://gmh.consellodacultura.org/">Gallaeciae Monumenta Historica</a> – An on-line repository of medieval texts <span class="languageicon">(in Galician)</span></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://cantigas.fcsh.unl.pt/index.asp">Cantigas Medievais Galego-Portuguesas</a> – A complete DB, containing the totality of the medieval profane lyric. <span class="languageicon">(in Portuguese)</span></li>
